25th August 2006.

Hon. Sperker,Parliament,Kotte.

Dear Sir,

POST OF DEPUTY CHAIRNAM OF COMMITTEES

I have tendered my resignation from the above post of His Excel-lency the President.

I hereby convey my sincere gratitude to yourself and all other staffMembers of Parliment for the Cooperation extended to me during myperiod as the Deputy Chairman of Committees of Parliament.

I look forward to your continued support in my future endeavors inand outside Parliament.

Thanking You,Yours faithfully,

M. Satchithananthan, M.P.Member of Parliament for Badulla District.

asked the Minister of Trade, Commerce, Consumer Affairsand Marketing Development and Minister of Highways,—

(a) Is he aware that,—

(i) a 12’x15’ sheet shed has been erected by one K.P.E.Jayasinghe of Ihalagama on a private land inWeweldeniya West, No. 20, Grama NiladhariDivision in the Mirigama Divisional Secretary’sDivision, outside the Urban DevelopmentAuthority, limits, opposite the Ceylon PetroleumCorporation fronting the Colombo - Kandy Road.

(iii) a person by the name of L. Niroshan has put up anunauthorized building in a land belonging to theRoad Development Authority reservationadjoining the aforesaid place;

(iv) a permit has been issued for obtaining electricitysupply to the aforesaid unauthorised building?

(b) Will he inform this House the reason for the RoadDevelopment Authority Engineer of Nittambuwa toissue orders to give a permit for an unauthorizedbuilding in a land reservation and to remove atemporary stall erected on a private land in the samevillage?

(c) If not, why?

asked the Prime Minister, Minister of Internal Administrationand Deputy Minister of Defence,—

(a) Will he inform this House,—

(i) whether the Lanka Marine Services (Private)Limited (LMS), which is a company engaged inthe business of supplying fuel to ships in theColombo Port, had belonged to the CeylonPetroleum Corporation;

(ii) whether 90% of shares of the aforesaid companywas sold to John Keels Holdings (Private) Limitedon 20.08.2002; and

(iii) the amount of money paid by the said John KeelsHoldings (Private) Limited to the Government forthis purpose?

(b) Will he state whether—

(i) the bid forwarded by the Sri Lanka ShippingLimited was rejected by the Technical AdvisoryCommittee on account of the fact that a monopolyfor a period of 8 years had been requested.

(ii) a perpetual monopoly was granted to the LankaMarine Services (Private) Limited in terms of theagreement signed by the Government at the timeof selling 90% of its shares;

(iii) the cabinet approval was granted for this; and

(iv) this company was granted the BOI - approved statusand a five-year tax waiver?

(c) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Enterprise Development andInvestment Promotion,—

(a) Will he submit to this House,—

(i) the number of Business Process OutsourceCompanies operating in Colombo; and

(ii) the companies came into Sri Lanka for the last sixmonths?

(ii) if not, the actions taken to remedy the situation?

asked the Minister of Education,—

(a) Will he submit separately to this House,—

(i) the total number of students who were selected atdistrict level for the medical, dental, veterinaryand engineering courses to the Universities of SriLanka from 1993 to 2005;

(ii) the number of students selected on the merit basisand the percentage;

(iii) the number of students selected under the districtquota system and the percentage;

(iv) the number of students selected under the difficultdistrict basis and the percentage?

(b) Will he state the annual growth rate in respect of eachof the above years in admitting students for each ofthe above courses?

(c) Will he submit to this House, the district level growthrate in relation to the increase in the number of stu-dents, in selecting students for the aforesaid coursesrespectively?

(d) If not, why?

It is against the Constitution. How can you work againstthe Constitution? Sir, I rise to a point of Order.

¦Íú ïÄïÌà Ì¿Í¾à ¨Ç ºøïÂ¾Éå:

“(3) Whenever the office of Speaker, Deputy Speaker or DeputyChairman of Committees becomes vacant otherwise than as a result ofa dissolution of Parliament, Parliament shall at its first meeting after theoccurrence of the vacancy elect another Member to be the Speaker, theDeputy Speaker or the Deputy Chairman of Committees, as the casemay be.”

You cannot act against the Constitution.

ªÇæ ÇÉêÏà Í¨ù ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ½Á[¹Æ Ä¯Æ¯ÉºÆ)(The Hon. Rauff Hakeem)Mr. Speaker, the convention in this House, the practice inthis House, to suspend Standing Orders had always been tovary the number of Members of Standing Committees orSelect Committees after discussion at the Party LeadersMeeting or to extend hours of Sittings or to discuss anymatter of public importance, putting aside GovernmentBusiness. These were the reasons for which we have beensuspending the Standing Orders usually as a practice in thisHouse.

Now in order to get over the problem that the Hon. JeyarajFernandopulle very correctly brought to the notice of theHouse about contravening the Constitution itself in tryingto elect a Member he himself suggested a way out, becausehe has to satisfy the JVP that he is not acting against theirinterests; perhaps so. But then I very earnestly tell you,Mr. Speaker, we are about to trample upon the right tofranchise in the House by doing this. Of course, he wantedthe Opposition to nominate a name. The Opposition isreluctant because they expected this matter to have beendiscussed with them. So, unfortunately now in order to getover one problem we are creating another problem.

Then there is also the other matter where at the PartyLeaders’ Meeting we came to an agreement to elect anotherMember and after coming to the House, the Government istrying to do something else. But the agreement at the PartyLeaders’ Meeting was to elect the Hon. Piyasiri Wijenayaketemporarily to the position.

That is what we are asking the Opposition whether theyare going to nominate a Member or not? They are notreplying this question.

ªÇæ ¦. ¡åÚ. ºòÀåÈ ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ©±Æ° ¤¼Æ° ºÈ¶Æ¶È¼¹Ç¾)(The Hon. H. R. Mithrapala)§ÂºëÄå Ä´ ¨øÆ¾à¾ ¢¶ ï¼¾à¾. ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ´ ÛÌà Éê¸ ÀÎÄê Éæ¾ø¡ÉÌà»åï ¾øïÆåà°ñ ¨åÇ¨ ÌÃåÀºøºëÄå ïºåàÇ¾à¾ ¡ÉÊñ ¾øÌå §ÂºëÄå´ÀêÝÉ¾à ¦à Ìà»åÉÇ ¾øïÆåàªÆ regulate ¨Ç¾à¾. Residuary powersÆ´ïºà; 142 Éæ¾ø Ìà»åÉÇ ¾øïÆåàªÆ Æ´ïºà §ÂºëÄå´ ÂÈºÈ ºøïÂ¾Éå.

¨»å¾åÆ¨ºëÄå(±¹Ç·Ç»¯¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(Mr. Speaker)ªÇæ ï®å¨àÌè Ä¾àºòéºëÄå.

ªÇæ ï¨à. ¦¾à. ï®å¨àÌè ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ Í¯° ©° Ì±Ç¯Æ)(The Hon. K. N. Choksy)Mr. Speaker, might I be permitted to point this out? For thepurpose of suspending the Standing Orders, the giving ofnotice is a mandatory requirement. It is a mandatoryrequirement. You cannot suspend unless notice is given evenif the proposal is made by a Minister. If the proposal is madeby a Minister, the only difference under Standing OrderNo.135 is this. The manner of determination of whether thereis a majority or not is affected. There is a special provisionmade as to how you decide whether a majority is in favour ofthe suspension or not. But, the giving of notice is a mandatoryrequirement. A notice has to be given and it has to be in theOrder Paper. Unless that is given, there is a violation ofStanding Order No. 135 because that is a mandatoryrequirement. If a Minister proposes it, then the next questionis, how to decide whether there is a majority or not? For that,there is a special provision. But even if a Minister makes aproposal, the requirement to give notice is not done awaywith. That is mandatory. I am referring to Standing OrderNo.135.

¨»å¾åÆ¨ºëÄå(±¹Ç·Ç»¯¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(Mr. Speaker)ÄÄ ¦à ÂÉ ºÄÆú Ì¿Í¾à ¨ïÎà; 135 É¾ Ìà»åÉÇ ¾øïÆåàªÆ ¡¾êÉ ¡ÉÊñ¼æ¾êè ¼ûÄ¨à ¼û ¾æº ¨øÆÈå ºÄÆú ÄÄ Ì¿Í¾à ¨ïÎà. [Âå½å ¨ø×]

ªÇæ °Æ¼åÌ Çå°À¨àË ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ²»¶Ç± ¼Ç²¹¯ÆÂ)(The Hon. Wijeyadasa Rajapaksa)

Sir, I rise to a point of Order. As Mr. Speaker pointed out inthe morning, these Standing Orders had been made byexercising the powers vested by the Constitution and allthese Standing Orders have to be interpreted subject to theprovisions of the Constitution. In the Constitution, it is saidthat whenever Parliament sits after the occurrence of thevacancy, we have to elect a Deputy Chairman of Committees.It had occurred yesterday or the day before and we are sittingtoday for the first time. Therefore, one cannot argue that theprovisions in Standing Order No. 23 shall supersede theConstitutional provisions. It is not possible at all. Therefore,since the Constitution says that you have to do it immediatelyafter the vacancy occurs, the question of giving seven days’notice will not arise at all. Therefore, we will have to act uponthe Constitution. Proper notice has been given by one of theHon. Ministers who is present in the House. So, we will haveto proceed with that.

Thank you.

III

Subscription : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available forRs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to theSUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATION BUREAU, No. 32, Transworks House,Lotus Road, Colombo 1. The fee should reach him on or bvefore November 30 each year.Late application for subscriptions will not be accepted.
